    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_553838">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/553838" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/47809-ryan" class="left imgcol" title="Ryan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1175607989p2/47809.jpg" alt="Ryan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/553838?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 18, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/47809-ryan" class="user" title="Ryan">Ryan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">see review</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/47809-ryan?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/47809-ryan?shelf=arthurian" class="actionLinkLite">arthurian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer553838">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7354612546781793578">I really can't say enough about this book. There are a lot of reasons to enjoy books and this one scores highest in so many categories. It is just very fun to read.<br /><br /><strong>Who would I recommend this book to?</strong><br /><strong>If you loved</strong> The <a title=" Lord of the Rings" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Lord%20of%20the%20Rings"> Lord of the Rings</a> but the smallest part of you that doesn't care about poetry kind of wished it had a little more action . . .<br /><strong>If you loved</strong> watching the movie <strong>Braveheart</strong> but wish it was a little more accurate historically . . .<br /><strong>If you were excited</strong> about the 2004 movie <strong>King Arthur</strong>, whi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7354612546781793578">I really can't say enough about this book. There are a lot of reasons to enjoy books and this one scores highest in so many categories. It is just very fun to read.<br /><br /><strong>Who would I recommend this book to?</strong><br /><strong>If you loved</strong> The <a title=" Lord of the Rings" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Lord%20of%20the%20Rings"> Lord of the Rings</a> but the smallest part of you that doesn't care about poetry kind of wished it had a little more action . . .<br /><strong>If you loved</strong> watching the movie <strong>Braveheart</strong> but wish it was a little more accurate historically . . .<br /><strong>If you were excited</strong> about the 2004 movie <strong>King Arthur</strong>, which although was advertised to be "the real story of King Arthur" had Arthur and his band of Mongolians defending the <em>Scottish</em> border against <em>Saxons</em>. The hell kind of sense does that make? Saxons invaded the South west coast, the region of England now called Saxony, the people Arthur would have fought on the Scottish border were, yes, you guessed it <em>Scotts</em> . . . <br /><strong>If you were excited</strong> ditto <strong>Tristan and Isolde</strong> . . .<br /><strong>If you loved</strong> <a title=" Robert Jordan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Robert%20Jordan"> Robert Jordan</a>'s <a title=" Wheel of Time" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Wheel%20of%20Time"> Wheel of Time</a> series but don't have the eons required to read each with a 1000+ pages per volume . . .<br /><br />I'll break down the idea behind the book. Yes, it's about King Arthur. And I know what you are thinking, "it's a magic book". <strong>No!</strong> there are no fairies, no pixie dust, no <a title=" Crystal Cave" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Crystal%20Cave"> Crystal Cave</a> (sorry <a title=" Mary Stewart" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Mary%20Stewart"> Mary Stewart</a> I loved your books too, but for slightly different reasons). The book does a real, <em>researched</em> job in telling a story which might have happened. Many of the characters believe in magic and things happen which might be interpreted as such but they might also be explained by realistic means.<br /><br />It portrays Arthur as a warlord in around 500 AD right after the Romans abandoned their foothold in the British Isles and right before the Anglo-Saxon invasion turned the Celtic land of Britain into Angl-land (England). History indicates something stopped the Saxon invasion for about 50 years and most historians believe that might have been Arthur. There is also no jousting (a sport popular about 700 years later). The story is different from the traditional Arthur Legend but similar enough to make it enjoyable to people who also liked:<br /><a title=" The Crystal Cave" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20The%20Crystal%20Cave"> The Crystal Cave</a><br /><a title=" The Once and Future King" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20The%20Once%20and%20Future%20King"> The Once and Future King</a><br /><a title=" Le Morte d'Arthur" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Le%20Morte%20d%27Arthur"> Le Morte d'Arthur</a><br />and the many hundreds of others, film and book.<br /><br />Oh, and I don't know who wrote the description which accompanies this book (probably someone at [<a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com" target="_blank">www.amazon.com</a>] but they say it is written in "flat American diction". I don't believe <a title=" Bernard Cornwell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Bernard%20Cornwell"> Bernard Cornwell</a>, a native of Britain, would appreciate that. He might live in America currently but is still quite English. What they may have meant to say is that it is "readable". Why they didn't just say that I have no idea.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7354612546781793578">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_929520046">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/929520046" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/27788046-bookworm-sean" class="left imgcol" title="Bookworm Sean"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1408905793p2/27788046.jpg" alt="Bookworm Sean" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/929520046?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 15, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/27788046-bookworm-sean" class="user" title="Bookworm Sean">Bookworm Sean</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/826595.The_Winter_King" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140231861" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/27788046-bookworm-sean?shelf=historical" class="actionLinkLite">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer929520046">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9458184466364476132">Nobody does this quite as well as Bernard Cornwell. He is quite literally the master of this genre. He creates a vivid warrior culture time and time again, and I will never get bored of it. This is saying a lot because Bernard Cornwell has written a huge amount of novels over the years and a few are similar in ways, but I don’t care because they’re just so good. This time Bernard Cornwell tells the story of Arthur, though not from the perspective of Arthur; he tells it from the point of view of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9458184466364476132">Nobody does this quite as well as Bernard Cornwell. He is quite literally the master of this genre. He creates a vivid warrior culture time and time again, and I will never get bored of it. This is saying a lot because Bernard Cornwell has written a huge amount of novels over the years and a few are similar in ways, but I don’t care because they’re just so good. This time Bernard Cornwell tells the story of Arthur, though not from the perspective of Arthur; he tells it from the point of view of one of his footman. <br /><br /><strong> An interesting take on the Arthurian myth </strong><br /><br />Derfel is a spearman in the service of Arthur and he narrates Arthur’s story. I’m glad that we weren’t privy to Arthur’s thoughts and emotion because it helped to create an idea about him being an untouchable being. What I mean is that Arthur is better than the common man, and by telling the story like this it assumes a sense of distance between someone like Derfel, who in himself is honourable, and someone who is, in essence, a man beyond measure. It created an Arthur that was as enigmatic as he was courageous and noble. I think it was a great idea. <br /><br />This is an awakening change to what I thought would be the predictable route of a novel like this. We see the events, and people, that surround Arthur’s life from a different perspective. One that holds Arthur in high esteem, but in spite of this, we also see the mistakes Arthur makes as a commander. He takes the wrong bride in a moment of selfish passion and almost dooms himself in the process. I emphasise the word mistakes because this is not the usual Camelot fairy tale; this is a gritty realistic approach to the legend. <br /><br /><strong> More historical than legend </strong><br /><br /><img width="400" height="400" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/photos/1439539316p8/1222367.jpg" /><br /><br />This is a tale that has been told countless times, but to make it stand out Cornwell had to make his retelling unique. In his version Lancelot is a fraud and Guinevere is quite possibly a complete whore who entrapped Arthur for power, not love; thus, this is far from the usual fairy tale. The characters are realistic and not without their flaws, so they are human and fallible. This is a far shot form the knights of the round table and the pure virtuous that Arthur represents. This made this novel not remotely predictable or a simple regurgitation of a tale we already know. <br /><br />The movement of Christianity through the reduction of the druids is also apparent. It is intriguing to see the rivalries created by these religious differences. I like the way the Druid’s, though relying on and believing in magic, appear to have no magical abilities but are driven by what they perceive as their magic powers and knowledge. I think Cornwell has been very subtle here because without openly suggesting that their magic was impossible, he does show us that their magic is slowly fading. This gives the novel a more realistic setting, a more historical setting, rather than the usual fantastical nature of tales surrounding Arthur Pendragon. <br /><br />I enjoyed this novel, but not as much as those in the Saxon Stories. Derfel lacks the charisma and will of Uhtred. And for that reason I gave this a four star rating rather than the five it could have earnt. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9458184466364476132">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer903095016215377171">This is my favorite Cornwell series (it's Cornwell's too), for it covers my favorite historical era--that mysterious gap in between the Roman departure and the Saxon Invasion. This retelling of Arthur works so well because it's divorced from Mallory. <br /><br />I love BC's ability to pull me into the muddy, primitive Dark Age Britain world. He's one of the very best at avoiding anachronisms, a skill which gets so little praise. None of his characters feel like modernistic men and women dressed up in 5th Ce</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText903095016215377171">This is my favorite Cornwell series (it's Cornwell's too), for it covers my favorite historical era--that mysterious gap in between the Roman departure and the Saxon Invasion. This retelling of Arthur works so well because it's divorced from Mallory. <br /><br />I love BC's ability to pull me into the muddy, primitive Dark Age Britain world. He's one of the very best at avoiding anachronisms, a skill which gets so little praise. None of his characters feel like modernistic men and women dressed up in 5th Century garb. They fear the powers of magic, gods, and fate. The majority of the people are ignorant, living in dirty hovels with no boots. The world is vast and mysterious. <br /><br />The line-by-line writing is excellent, as are the story arcs of this tale. <br /><br />Highly suggest this series, as well as most of BC's work. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_954277477">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/954277477" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/30552336-conor" class="left imgcol" title="Conor"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1400278909p2/30552336.jpg" alt="Conor" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/954277477?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/30552336-conor" class="user" title="Conor">Conor</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=awesome-books-are-awesome" class="actionLinkLite">awesome-books-are-awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer954277477">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4525293396261968754">4.5 stars <br /><br />The legend of Arthur has been told time and again over the centuries. From ancient British folk tales to 5 season of 'Merlin', from 15th Century French verse to 'The Mists of Avalon'. With this book Cornwell has left his mark on that tradition. He's taken a tale examined from almost every angle and made it his own. Most of all he's written a story filled with complicated characters, visceral battles and ambitious intrigues in a brutal, immersive setting. <br /><br />The protagonist of this story i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4525293396261968754">4.5 stars <br /><br />The legend of Arthur has been told time and again over the centuries. From ancient British folk tales to 5 season of 'Merlin', from 15th Century French verse to 'The Mists of Avalon'. With this book Cornwell has left his mark on that tradition. He's taken a tale examined from almost every angle and made it his own. Most of all he's written a story filled with complicated characters, visceral battles and ambitious intrigues in a brutal, immersive setting. <br /><br />The protagonist of this story is Derfel Cadarn. A humble, straight-forward soldier Derfel is in a position to observe the complicated characters involved in the military and political struggles to decide the fate, and faith (lol @ puns) of Britain. Derfel also gives us an engaging insight into the terror and exhilaration of fighting in a shield wall. These sections, which bring to life the mud, blood, exhaustion, fear and pain of frontline combat are some of the most intense of the book. The framing device, with Derfal now an old monk telling his story, created some extremely poignant moments.<br /><br />Arthur is extremely well-written, although his character sometimes feels too noble, especially given how bleak the rest of this world is. To be fair, Arthurian legend usually holds Arthur up as the pinnacle of all that is right and in this series Cornwell portrays him as the one hope for goodness in a world filled with evil. For all of his saintliness (although saints in this book are often knobs Coughs* Sansum Coughs*) Arthur's vanity, ambition and occasional reckless idealism made him more than a 2-D representation of heroism and instead showed him to be a flawed, realistic character, making his struggles all the more powerful. <br /><br />In the early stages of this book I found Owain (the old king's champion) to be a brilliantly written character, a complex villain and a great source of conflict. On one hand Owain was a great warrior who was generous and kind to the men under his command (including Derfal) on the other hand he was openly corrupt, raped a captive woman (this was a disturbingly frequent occurrence in the story, at times the frequency of rape went beyond realistic in this setting and into being gratuitous) and mercilessly slaughtered a defenceless village to line his own pockets. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ Due to his scummy actions I didn't find him an overly sympathetic character, as a result his death pretty early on didn't really affect me. However as the book progressed I felt his absence more keenly, especially as a bunch of much less compelling villains began to appear. I also thought that Derfal suddenly siding against him and his abrupt death cut out what could have been a really interesting contest for Derfal's loyalty between Owain's pragmatism (represented by his faith in the shield-wall) and Arthur's idealism (his love of heavy cavalry) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />In contrast Lancelot was a character with all the depth and complexity of a WWE villain (or 'heel' for those of you in the know...). Lancelot was shown to be vain, cowardly, arrogant, bullying and manipulative. Cornwell made a few half-hearted attempts at making him sympathetic and realistic but vague references to him only being a tool to Derfal because he fears him and his kindness to people who don't threaten him were never actually shown in the text and as a result don't have any real impact. In any situation he could be counted on to do the worst thing possible and this lack of complexity made the absence of Owain all the more obvious. <br /><br />The setting in this book, often stark and bleak, was brought to life brilliantly. The violence, turmoil and savagery of Dark Ages Britain were captured perfectly. Cornwell captured this sense of danger even better than Iggulden in 'Genghis'. The impact of religion was explored intelligently in this book as well. The conflict between druidism and Christianity and the effect it had on politics was well-handled. The presence of other cults and sects in the background served to give the portrayal of religion even more depth and to further ingrain it in the world. I did struggle with the use of magic in this book however. Magic, especially druids, play a major role in this story however the fact that all of this 'magic' is so obviously a sham made it's frequent, and supposedly threatening, use seem ridiculous. The behaviour of druids and other 'mage' types throughout the plot bordered on comical and the characters' naiveté to these obvious hoaxes was frustrating. <br /><br />Overall this story was a great example of historical fiction and a unique and powerful retelling of the Legend of Arthur. I'm definitely going to continue on with this series.<br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4525293396261968754">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_480818034">

  <a href="/user/show/6803829-nate" class="left imgcol" title="Nate"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1413944642p2/6803829.jpg" alt="Nate" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/480818034?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 19, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6803829-nate" class="user" title="Nate">Nate</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6803829-nate?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6803829-nate?shelf=middle-ages" class="actionLinkLite">middle-ages</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6803829-nate?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6803829-nate?shelf=creeps-perverts-psychos-killers" class="actionLinkLite">creeps-perverts-psychos-killers</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer480818034">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3982467012240529671">I haven't read all of Cornwell's books but from what I've read this is my absolute favorite so far. It's a fantastic vision of what Arthur's life might have really been like. The typical idea that seems to stick in people's heads is of this romantic story with gallant knights, fair maidens and all that boring stuff but when you think about it, there really was no room in the post-Roman Dark Ages Britain for that kind of shit. Don't get me wrong, there's plenty of heroism in this book but it's mo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3982467012240529671">I haven't read all of Cornwell's books but from what I've read this is my absolute favorite so far. It's a fantastic vision of what Arthur's life might have really been like. The typical idea that seems to stick in people's heads is of this romantic story with gallant knights, fair maidens and all that boring stuff but when you think about it, there really was no room in the post-Roman Dark Ages Britain for that kind of shit. Don't get me wrong, there's plenty of heroism in this book but it's more the exception than the rule (and that's what made it so stirring for me). People are just fucking mean, cowardly, deceitful and sadistic in this book but that's what makes Arthur shine so brilliantly. On the other side of that coin, however, Cornwell writes him as a real person with flaws and failures. This depth extends to most of the rest of the characters.<br /><br />One of the things I really liked about the Saxon books is the sketchy, creepy magic-related stuff (I'm thinking of scenes particularly in, uh...I think <em>Lords of the North</em> and <em>Death of Kings</em>) and this is even more brilliantly realized in this book. As you'd expect, the "magic" in these books always turns out to be elaborate human trickery but the characters believe in it so fervently that it creates this spooky atmosphere and you really can see how real it was to these people. The Isle of the Dead, the Druids, all of the weird pagan rituals...good stuff.<br /><br />This book was just so full of memorable scenes, characters, locations...it really seems like Cornwell was really inspired when he wrote this one. I have extremely high hopes for the following two books of the trilogy. Even though I know what has to eventually happen it's still gripping reading for me. At this point, this seems like it's probably Cornwell's masterpiece. It goes above and beyond being "just" an adventure story.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3982467012240529671">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_258670094">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258670094" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7356331-magdalena" class="left imgcol" title="Magdalena"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1391307523p2/7356331.jpg" alt="Magdalena" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/258670094?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7356331-magdalena" class="user" title="Magdalena">Magdalena</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7297518-the-winter-king" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7356331-magdalena?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7356331-magdalena?shelf=myths-legends" class="actionLinkLite">myths-legends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer258670094'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer258670094">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3047999216973585191">So everyone knows about the Arthurian legends and that there isn't much historical evidence (if any) that Arthur existed. That said, this book strikes me as an accurate account of what it would have been like if such a warlord lived. The historical setting- Saxon raids, Irish conquerors, religious disputes, traces of Roman civilization, all that good stuff, is pretty accurate. Bernard Cornwell evidently did serious research into the way of life in 500ad, and it all gives a very authentic vibe. T</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3047999216973585191">So everyone knows about the Arthurian legends and that there isn't much historical evidence (if any) that Arthur existed. That said, this book strikes me as an accurate account of what it would have been like if such a warlord lived. The historical setting- Saxon raids, Irish conquerors, religious disputes, traces of Roman civilization, all that good stuff, is pretty accurate. Bernard Cornwell evidently did serious research into the way of life in 500ad, and it all gives a very authentic vibe. Things are portrayed as they were, with warriors wearing light armor to be more agile, Saxons wearing simple and crude armor (I absolutely praise the lack of impractical yet fancy demon-horned helmets), druids spiking their hair with dung, the lack of actual magic, and much more humanized characters.<br /><br />The narrator, Derfel Cadarn, is old and feeble, retelling Arthur's story to the current young queen Igraine. At this point (Book #1), some parts of the story are compromised due to his own beliefs (as pointed out by Igraine). Chiefly, his hatred towards Lancelot and the accusations of cowardice, and the praise to the Star of Powys and her beauty. We can't know if his descriptions are somewhat biased in some aspects, but that makes for an entertaining story. (On a lesser note, I also quite enjoyed Igraine's impatience to know what happens in the end, for I felt the same way. Derfel, however, kept the story linear, without jumping to spoilers, much to her discontent.)<br /><br />The main character, Arthur, is a very decent fellow. He empathizes with everyone (and by everyone I do mean everyone. Except Saxons.) and tries to be fair in judgement, tactful, respectful, brave, and honorable. Perhaps his major flaws are his love of Guinevere, his stubbornness, and his ambition. His ultimate goal is to unite Britain against foreign invasions and to secure his protegee the throne of Dumnonia, while leading that peace himself. Despite all this, he insults Powys by first betrothing the powisian princess and then abruptly marrying Guinevere out of mad, passionate, foolish love. (Lust?) And so the ultimate war begins, facing enemies on all sides- Franks fighting Armorica on the south (a kingdom Arthur had sworn to protect), Irish Blackshields and Kernow on the west, Siluria and Powys on the north, and Saxons on the East. War and madness all over the place, how much more real can this time period get? <br /><br />In the legends Merlin is a majestic, wise, kind even, Druid. In the book I thought he was more of a scumbag, using everyone for his own amusement, not caring for peoples' suffering. But yes, he was wise and feared by all, with the impatience at people's stupidity that I guess could only come with the knowledge and power he possessed. All in all, I liked him.<br /><br />As for a minor pet peeve, there is a ton of spit in this book. Everyone spits at everyone to insult them, to ward off evil, to release some anger, to prove a point, to curse... You get the idea.<br /><br />In conclusion, excellent, excellent book. Had me surprised at reading so much so suddenly without even realizing how much I had read. Recommended to people who want a realistic legend, who enjoy the Dark Ages, who like accurate historical settings, who believe chivalry shouldn't be dead, and who like ancient battles. I for one, am absolutely thrilled to read the next book in this series :)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3047999216973585191">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_94742121">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94742121" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/545336-mike" class="left imgcol" title="Mike"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1329191662p2/545336.jpg" alt="Mike" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/94742121?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 16, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/545336-mike" class="user" title="Mike">Mike</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/120287.The_Winter_King" title="Hardcover 9780312144470" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=history" class="actionLinkLite">history</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=xcharity-2012" class="actionLinkLite">xcharity-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer94742121">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7666471478333462255">TWK <a title="The Winter King (The Arthur Books, #1) by Bernard Cornwell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68520.The_Winter_King__The_Arthur_Books___1_"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="The Winter King (The Arthur Books, #1) by Bernard Cornwell" src="http://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1311987677s/68520.jpg" /></a> is easy 5 stars for bringing this oft-told tale to us in a completely new (and I do mean new) way. <strong>WARNING! Do Not read this book if you like your Arthur legend gauzy, frilly, magicky and cheesy.</strong> All previous Arthurian tales pale in comparison to Mr. Cornwell’s version. All of the usual suspects are present here but you will not see many of them portrayed in the standard ways. You will also meet a host of new companions and enemies. It is safe to say that you will never look at Lancelot, G</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7666471478333462255">TWK <a title="The Winter King (The Arthur Books, #1) by Bernard Cornwell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68520.The_Winter_King__The_Arthur_Books___1_">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="The Winter King (The Arthur Books, #1) by Bernard Cornwell" src="http://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1311987677s/68520.jpg" /></a> is easy 5 stars for bringing this oft-told tale to us in a completely new (and I do mean new) way. <strong>WARNING! Do Not read this book if you like your Arthur legend gauzy, frilly, magicky and cheesy.</strong> All previous Arthurian tales pale in comparison to Mr. Cornwell’s version. All of the usual suspects are present here but you will not see many of them portrayed in the standard ways. You will also meet a host of new companions and enemies. It is safe to say that you will never look at Lancelot, Guinevere and Morgan in the same light. Arthur is completely believable as a real person. While he is noble and also fallible, this Arthur is an implacable and ruthless warrior when needed. You will care for the new characters in Arthur’s service and despise his fiendish enemies. Merlin is a real treat, never easily categorized. Mordred is despicable in a way that makes sense.<br /><br />This first book in the trilogy introduces Arthur as he tries to stop the Britons fighting each other and unite them to oppose the invading Saxons. Some of the venues are familiar and some are not. You will meet and follow Derfel, who tells the tale long after it occurred, and he is a central and appealing character.<br /><br />What sets this story apart is Cornwell’s attempt to show a realistic portrayal of what a Welsh Arthur would have been like. He also tries to show what life was like at the time. (If you need vowels to pronounce names and words, you will be struggling. His characters often have names like the trolls in Tolkien’s tales and the place names look like sites in Mordor.) While Cornwell states up front this is not his attempt to write a true history, it becomes so realistic you will think it must have been so.<br /><br />The Winter King is set in a cold, dreary time when the Britons are fighting each other while the Saxons slowly invade the eastern part of the island. There is a recognition that the glories of Roman civilization, learning and progress are fading and that the Britons cannot build on that legacy. A long dark period is looming. Adding to this mix is a war between Christianity and paganism. It isn’t pretty but Cornwell’s story is so rich and pungent, I found myself caring for these characters like few others I have ever read. You will too.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7666471478333462255">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/8386404-richard" class="left imgcol" title="Richard"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1351707681p2/8386404.jpg" alt="Richard" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1144378173?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 07, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8386404-richard" class="user" title="Richard">Richard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1144378173">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8131194341687175456">7.5/10<br /><br />It took a while for me to get into this, I was overwhelmed with the amount of names thrust at me from the off. From the start you've learnt more characters names in the first few pages than most series will have in their entire run only for the majority of these to be killed off before you've remembered who they are! Luckily, things steadied after a while and you had a core group and things became more focused and the story was able to really progress.<br /><br />I guess the story of King Arthur and M</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8131194341687175456">7.5/10<br /><br />It took a while for me to get into this, I was overwhelmed with the amount of names thrust at me from the off. From the start you've learnt more characters names in the first few pages than most series will have in their entire run only for the majority of these to be killed off before you've remembered who they are! Luckily, things steadied after a while and you had a core group and things became more focused and the story was able to really progress.<br /><br />I guess the story of King Arthur and Merlin and his knights is quite well know but the more I read the more I realised I knew very little actually other than the sword and a few of the knights names which made for a more entertaining read as I had no idea who would do what or who would meet a grisly doom.<br /><br />Cornwell has a tendency to stick in massive descriptive passages which I personally struggled with at times. However, even with that said, I noticed at the latter stages of the book I found myself thinking about the book when I wasn't reading it and I needed to know what happened next which is always a good sign. At the finish I was grateful that there are two more books in the series and hoping now all the main characters have been introduced the next book will get straight into things without introducing a list of people as long as the telephone book.<br /><br />If you like this try: "Azincourt" by Bernard Cornwell </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8131194341687175456">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_514153418">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/514153418" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1662632-richard" class="left imgcol" title="Richard"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428399194p2/1662632.jpg" alt="Richard" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/514153418?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 31, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1662632-richard" class="user" title="Richard">Richard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/120287.The_Winter_King" title="Hardcover 9780312144470" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer514153418">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12026023679193433536">This is the first of a trilogy in a magnificent telling of the Arthurian legend. Yeah, that one: Arthur, Merlin, Uther Pendragon, Guinevere, Morgan, Mordred, Lancelot, Galahad — the whole cast, as far as I know (well, Morgause appears to be missing).<br /><br />I haven’t read any of the others Arthurian books, so I can’t comment on any linkages between this and the agglomeration of other tellings. My knowledge of this history/legend/mythos comes mostly from what I’ve picked up here and there, with a heavy d</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12026023679193433536">This is the first of a trilogy in a magnificent telling of the Arthurian legend. Yeah, that one: Arthur, Merlin, Uther Pendragon, Guinevere, Morgan, Mordred, Lancelot, Galahad — the whole cast, as far as I know (well, Morgause appears to be missing).<br /><br />I haven’t read any of the others Arthurian books, so I can’t comment on any linkages between this and the agglomeration of other tellings. My knowledge of this history/legend/mythos comes mostly from what I’ve picked up here and there, with a heavy dose of Monty Python, Camelot (the musical) and fond-if-vague recollections of the dark 1981 movie, <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0082348/">Excalibur</a>.<br /><br />Bernard Cornwell relies on the point that what is “known” about Arthur is microscopic compared to the stories that have been told, and that gives him the leeway to tweak the legend in ways that aren’t available to most “historical” fiction. In other words, there is so much fiction already in the mixture that he can transpose the historical portion to where he thinks he will have the most fun. In his afterword, he admits that his choices are “capricious at best and fortified by the certainty that no real answer exists”. In the end, he locates his story in the part of Britain he loves best.<br /><br />The <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_arthur">Wikipedia page</a> on King Arthur tells us he was <em>possibly</em> a real human being around the early sixth century. This is long after the first Christian missionaries came to <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_Wales#History">Wales</a> and maybe after <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Druidism#Possible_late_survival_of_Insular_druidism">druidism was largely eliminated</a>. But in Cornwell’s tale, druids play an important role, which distinguishes this from the heavily Christianized tales that dominate the most popular tellings of Arthur (e.g., the Holy Grail — although the Grail does make an appearance, <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thirteen_Treasures_of_the_Island_of_Britain#The_Cauldron_of_Dyrnwch_the_Giant">sort of</a>).<br /><br />Many others parts of the story are also shifted a bit: the major characters don’t have the same relationships to one another — for example, Galahad is Lancelot’s illegitimate half-brother, not his illegitimate son. Mordred isn’t Arthur’s son, but nephew (and an infant in this first volume).<br /><br />The very first portion — fifty, maybe sixty pages? — is a little slow. Derfel Cadarn, the narrator is an old monk, writing this history. (He is based on the historical <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Derfel">Saint Derfel Gadarn</a>; the book is written in the first person from his perspective). As his tale begins, he is a young man of Saxon ancestry who had been adopted as an orphan by Merlin. Merlin is absent, and no one knows where he is, when he might return, or even if he is alive. The High King, Uther Pendragon, has sent his heir and grandson, Mordred, to Merlin’s camp at Ynys Wydryn.<br /><br />The barrage of Welsh (or Cornish, I’m not completely sure) words and names can be pretty overwhelming, and several times I was tempted to abandon the book and move on to something else. But eventually the situation becomes clear, and some action kicks in, and the for the rest of the book there is no question that we’re in the hands of a master storyteller.<br /><br />As the chapters go by, more of the expected Arthurian characters are added to the mix. Cornwell does an excellent job at making Arthur a complex character (Merlin remains mostly an enigma), torn between his belief that he can forge Britain into a unified people, able to resist the despised Saxons, and his passions; chief among them, the <em>femme fatale</em>, Guinevere. The politics certainly seems accurate. Perhaps the real draw is the military aspect: Cornwell gives us a real feel for what spear-and-shield fighting was about. Maintaining the <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shield_wall">shield wall</a> was paramount; as long as it stood your side would probably get by with few casualties, but woe to those facing the melee after it collapsed, especially if they had been flanked.<br /><br />I suspect someone could spend many hours tracking Cornwell’s usage of actual historical names and places. For example, the final battle in this book is at “Lugg Vale”, which was actually the site of a very similar fight in the early fifteenth century, the <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Bryn_Glas">Battle of Bryn Glas</a>. Thus, the “historical” half of “historical fiction” is well rooted.<br /><br />Since I’ve only read this first book in the trilogy, I can’t endorse the whole series, although I certainly plan on continuing into the next volume, and I can recommend <em>
  <strong>The Winter King</strong>
</em> to anyone who enjoys a rousing good story.<br />­</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12026023679193433536">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/113880236?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 10, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1956959-chris" class="user" title="Chris ">Chris </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer113880236">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3713978429131789611">Excellent novel. Cornwell has truly taken the Arthurian legend and made it his own. All the old names are here, but often in much different forms than expected.<br /><br />This tale is told by one of Arthur's warriors, Derfel. In his old age, Derfel has become a monk. While serving as such, he is writing the story of Arthur, who he knew personally.<br /><br />Cornwell's Arthur is a delight. While maintaining a degree of the larger-than-life qualities we come to expect of this character, Cornwell makes him human. Gives</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3713978429131789611">Excellent novel. Cornwell has truly taken the Arthurian legend and made it his own. All the old names are here, but often in much different forms than expected.<br /><br />This tale is told by one of Arthur's warriors, Derfel. In his old age, Derfel has become a monk. While serving as such, he is writing the story of Arthur, who he knew personally.<br /><br />Cornwell's Arthur is a delight. While maintaining a degree of the larger-than-life qualities we come to expect of this character, Cornwell makes him human. Gives him flaws. While he strives to realize his dream of a free, united Britain, his shortcomings often get in the way. Derfel sees his flaws and his loyalty does not waver. <br /><br />This is probably the most "real" I've seen an Arthurian story done, due to the way Cornwell handles his characters. Some are heroic, some are villainous. Some go both ways. But they all have a human element that gives them authenticity. <br /><br />There are two more books in the series, and though this one left off at a good pause point, I'll certainly be seeking those out.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_55204461">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55204461" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2232084-kate-quinn" class="left imgcol" title="Kate Quinn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1322689147p2/2232084.jpg" alt="Kate Quinn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/55204461?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 14, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2232084-kate-quinn" class="user" title="Kate Quinn">Kate Quinn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer55204461">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3025891375734445936">Hands down the best King Arthur fiction ever written. "The Winter King" begins Bernard Cornwell's trilogy of Arthur, the king who may have lived in early Britain, driven back the invading Saxons, and inspired a legend. Interestingly enough, Arthur is not the central hero of the book - that role falls to Derfel, a Saxon boy who escapes a Druid death pit to be raised by Britons and eventually become Arthur's right-hand man. Derfel is a very old man when the story begins, a monk in a Christian mona</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3025891375734445936">Hands down the best King Arthur fiction ever written. "The Winter King" begins Bernard Cornwell's trilogy of Arthur, the king who may have lived in early Britain, driven back the invading Saxons, and inspired a legend. Interestingly enough, Arthur is not the central hero of the book - that role falls to Derfel, a Saxon boy who escapes a Druid death pit to be raised by Britons and eventually become Arthur's right-hand man. Derfel is a very old man when the story begins, a monk in a Christian monastery who is writing the story of the leader he followed all his life. We meet Derfel as a boy, dreaming of becoming a warrior someday and in love with his Druid-in-training friend Nimue. The land is ruled by a baby king, Mordred, and is soon torn apart by war. Arthur rides to the rescue (Mordred is his nephew rather than his son; expect deviations from the normal Arthur myths) and Derfel wants nothing more than to serve him. Derfel will grow up, become a warrior, fall in love a few times, and eventually stand at Arthur's side in a cataclysmic war that begins when Arthur spurns a princess to marry a penniless beauty named Guinevere. "The Winter King" starts rather slowly - Cornwell admits he got too interested in laying out the scene than proceeding with the story - but stick with it. This is some of the best historical fiction ever written. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3025891375734445936">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/914944782?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 29, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12348405-vagner-stefanello" class="user" title="Vagner Stefanello">Vagner Stefanello</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3025956-o-rei-do-inverno" title="Paperback 9788501061140" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/12348405-vagner-stefanello?shelf=physical" class="actionLinkLite">physical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer914944782">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13268421577525854897">Review in Portuguese from <a rel="nofollow" href="http://desbravandolivros.blogspot.com.br/2013/02/resenha-o-rei-do-inverno-bernard.html">Desbravando Livros</a>:<br /><br />Depois de tanto tempo, finalmente consegui começar a ler As Crônicas de Artur e descobrir se os livros são realmente bons como as pessoas falam por aí. O Rei do Inverno é o primeiro livro da trilogia de Bernard Cornwell e nos coloca na pele de Derfel Cadarn, filho de uma escrava saxã e atualmente aos cuidados do druida Merlin. Derfel (pronuncia-se Dervel) é introduzido em um cenário de guerra e várias disputadas pelo poder dentro da própria Grã-Bretan</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13268421577525854897">Review in Portuguese from <a rel="nofollow" href="http://desbravandolivros.blogspot.com.br/2013/02/resenha-o-rei-do-inverno-bernard.html">Desbravando Livros</a>:<br /><br />Depois de tanto tempo, finalmente consegui começar a ler As Crônicas de Artur e descobrir se os livros são realmente bons como as pessoas falam por aí. O Rei do Inverno é o primeiro livro da trilogia de Bernard Cornwell e nos coloca na pele de Derfel Cadarn, filho de uma escrava saxã e atualmente aos cuidados do druida Merlin. Derfel (pronuncia-se Dervel) é introduzido em um cenário de guerra e várias disputadas pelo poder dentro da própria Grã-Bretanha e passará por diversas provações ao longo do seu caminho.<br /><br /><em>"Eu me agachei, e todo o terror cresceu de novo dentro de mim. Minhas mãos estavam suando, a perna esquerda estava coçando, a garganta estava seca, eu queria vomitar, e minhas entranhas estavam líquidas. Hywel tinha me ensinado bem, mas eu nunca havia enfrentado um homem que quisesse me matar. Podia ouvir os homens que se aproximavam, mas não podia vê-los, e meu instinto mais forte era virar as costas e correr atrás das mulheres. Mas fiquei. Não tinha escolha. Desde a infância vinha ouvindo histórias de guerreiros e fora ensinado repetidamente que um homem nunca dava as costas e fugia. Um homem lutava por seu senhor, enfrentava o inimigo e nunca fugia."</em><br /><br />Em meio às dificuldades impostas pelo destino, nosso protagonista encontra vários guerreiros que serão seus leais companheiros ao longo da sua jornada, assim como traidores da pior espécie possível e diversas mulheres que fazem o seu coração bater mais forte. Essas partes de romance são bem distribuídas ao longo de todo o livro e aparecem nos momentos certos, pois as batalhas são o ponto forte dos livros do Bernard Cornwell e nada deve deixá-las em segundo plano.<br /><br />Há outra coisa que eu devo ressaltar antes de finalizar essa resenha: a descrição das paredes de escudos é simplesmente espetacular. O autor domina essa arte como ninguém e faz de tudo para inserir o próprio leitor em meio às lanças e escudos dos desbravadores no campo de batalha.<br /><br /><em>"Para mim, desesperado por ganhar um anel de guerreiro feito de ferro saxão, parecia loucura não atacarmos, mas eu ainda não havia experimentado a carnificina de duas paredes de escudos entrelaçadas, nem tinha aprendido como é difícil persuadir homens a oferecer seus corpos para esse trabalho macabro."</em><br /><br />O livro acaba prendendo a atenção do leitor durante toda a narrativa e tem um final de tirar o fôlego. Vale a pena apostar em Bernard Cornwell e conhecer melhor a história de Artur, Lancelot, Guinevere, Owain, Merlin e muitos outros.<br /><br /><strong>Pontos fortes:</strong> as descrições das paredes de escudos!<br /><strong>Pontos fracos:</strong> faltou dar um desenvolvimento melhor a alguns personagens da trama.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13268421577525854897">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It's written by Derfel, one Merlin's collected orphans. <br /><br />Derfel, who was one of Merlin's Tor and who became most trusted, brother-like to Arthur and Gallahad and many such good men, now is a follower of Christianity.<br /><br />He is one of the last of people left who remember King Arthur, other than the Saint who's Bishop of the Church he's sworn to stay in- Sansum.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText12735297690682014905">An Amazing Novel!<br /><br />This is a book about King Arthur (not King, but Warlock). It's written by Derfel, one Merlin's collected orphans. <br /><br />Derfel, who was one of Merlin's Tor and who became most trusted, brother-like to Arthur and Gallahad and many such good men, now is a follower of Christianity.<br /><br />He is one of the last of people left who remember King Arthur, other than the Saint who's Bishop of the Church he's sworn to stay in- Sansum. And he is only one who can write about the most hated by Christians, the Enemy of God- Arthur. He writes this book for Queen Igrain, while lying to Sansum that he's writing Gospels in Saxon tongue.<br /><br />The story leads as follows: <br />Derfel, now missing Merlin for 5 years, is trained as Clerk as well as his dream job- Knight.<br />Uther's son Mordred is dead, and he blames his bastard- Arthur for Mordred's death.<br /><br />Mordred's son is born atlast to Norweina. And Utger dies due to his old age! <br /><br />From here, strts Derfel's journey to Knighthood and an Amazing story about how the Kingdoms fought, enemies, friends, love, craze,war, Arthur, Merlin, Nimue, Guinevere, Lancelot, Galahad, etc.<br /><br />I loved this book and his writing!<br /><br />Who will love this? Lord of the Rings fans, people who want to learn more about Arthurian legend. Adventure, war-lovers woukd live this!<br /><br />My suggestion to all Fantasy and historical fiction lovers is- Read this!<br />Five stars!!!!</span>

        <a href="/review/show/418457462?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 18, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6751111-artemas" class="user" title="Artemas">Artemas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/826595.The_Winter_King" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140231861" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6751111-artemas?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6751111-artemas?shelf=medieval-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">medieval-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer418457462">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17302879644169500896"><em>*Please don’t label ME an Enemy of God for only rating this 3 stars.</em><br /><br />I’ve been a fan of Bernard Cornwell for some time now and believe him to be one of the best historical fiction writers out there. While I enjoyed this book, something about it just felt off to me, lacking that distinct Cornwellishness that I’ve come to love. <em>The Winter King</em> is a slow build, to be sure, but has some interesting payoffs along the way.<br /><br />The debate on whether or not Arthur ever existed is still undecided, but Cornwell</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17302879644169500896"><em>*Please don’t label ME an Enemy of God for only rating this 3 stars.</em><br /><br />I’ve been a fan of Bernard Cornwell for some time now and believe him to be one of the best historical fiction writers out there. While I enjoyed this book, something about it just felt off to me, lacking that distinct Cornwellishness that I’ve come to love. <em>The Winter King</em> is a slow build, to be sure, but has some interesting payoffs along the way.<br /><br />The debate on whether or not Arthur ever existed is still undecided, but Cornwell does an impressive job at making the reader believe that these characters, and the events surrounding them, were part of Britain’s history and not a simple fairy tale.<br /><br />It was tough deciding how to rate this book by giving it a 3 or 4 star rating. For me this is another case that Goodreads really needs half star ratings. In the end I felt more comfortable with a 3 star, but I also feel confident that the next books in the series will get better as the story progresses. <br /><br />Blood has been spilled, key pieces have been arranged, and the struggle for Britain continues.<br /></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/688899392?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 17, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4745220-alicja" class="user" title="Alicja">Alicja</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13113933-the-winter-king" title="Paperback 9780241955673" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=myths-legends" class="actionLinkLite">myths-legends</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=5th-16th-century" class="actionLinkLite">5th-16th-century</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=bookclub" class="actionLinkLite">bookclub</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=arthurian" class="actionLinkLite">arthurian</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=male-author" class="actionLinkLite">male-author</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=early-mid-ages-eu-500-1000" class="actionLinkLite">early-mid-ages-eu-500-1000</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=medieval" class="actionLinkLite">medieval</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=war-military-battle" class="actionLinkLite">war-military-battle</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=pre-gun-battles" class="actionLinkLite">pre-gun-battles</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=dream-library" class="actionLinkLite">dream-library</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=arec-for-t" class="actionLinkLite">arec-for-t</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer688899392">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11555785899756685860">rating: 5.5/5 <br /><br />Cornwell uses what little historical facts there are regarding the originator of the Arthurian legends and plays around with history to show us what could have been (meaning no magic). He freely admits that he had a lot of room to play and that this is just one interpretation, but damn, it's a brilliant interpretation. All the well knows characters are included (Arthur, Merlin, Lancelot, Guinevere, King Uther, Morgan, Galahad, etc.) but not necessarily as the legends describe them.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11555785899756685860">rating: 5.5/5 <br /><br />Cornwell uses what little historical facts there are regarding the originator of the Arthurian legends and plays around with history to show us what could have been (meaning no magic). He freely admits that he had a lot of room to play and that this is just one interpretation, but damn, it's a brilliant interpretation. All the well knows characters are included (Arthur, Merlin, Lancelot, Guinevere, King Uther, Morgan, Galahad, etc.) but not necessarily as the legends describe them.<br /><br />I adored this first part in the trilogy from almost the first page (I have to admit that the first 40 pages or so were a bit slow and had so many names and places I was a bit confused but it gets straightened out soon enough). <br /><br />Cornwell is a genius in depicting exciting and realistic battles (at least seemingly realistic to someone who has never fought a medieval battle herself). My pulse raced as swords and spears and shields clashed. But Cornwell doesn't sacrifice story or character development for the battles. All the major characters are fully and vividly drawn, making this a fast-paced and exciting romp through 5th century Britain while keeping the reader invested in the outcomes and stories.<br /><br />The story is told from the POV of Derfel (who I found is a lesser known knight of Arthur), living at a monastery during old age he decides to write down his story to set the record straight. I love Derfel; he is loyal yet morally conflicted about some of what he does for loyalty, he is in love with unattainable women yet he still loves them fully, he is brave but not without fear. And the relationships are just brilliant, Derfel is the perfect reflection of their personalities. And yet he is not unbiased, he loves and hates through his own interpretation so we are left with an incomplete picture, there always remaining something hidden, elusive living in the shadows. And Merlin is, well, the craziest Merlin I've ever read. Love, love, love Merlin!<br /><br />Can't wait to pick up the next novel in the trilogy!<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11555785899756685860">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/976133-robin" class="left imgcol" title="Robin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1408717563p2/976133.jpg" alt="Robin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/17304008?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 17, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/976133-robin" class="user" title="Robin">Robin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/976133-robin?shelf=arthurian-legend" class="actionLinkLite">arthurian-legend</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/976133-robin?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/976133-robin?shelf=england" class="actionLinkLite">england</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer17304008">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10857731110197717463">This book, along with the two that follow it, really break the mold when it comes to Arthurian legend. These stories are told much more factually, set against feudal Britain. The bit of magic that shows up doesn't dominate the story like all other Arthurian legend. It is much easier to picture this Arthur as having actually existed and the things that happen as having actually happened. It's not even told from the viewpoint of a character that we are used to seeing in King Arthur stories. It pai</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10857731110197717463">This book, along with the two that follow it, really break the mold when it comes to Arthurian legend. These stories are told much more factually, set against feudal Britain. The bit of magic that shows up doesn't dominate the story like all other Arthurian legend. It is much easier to picture this Arthur as having actually existed and the things that happen as having actually happened. It's not even told from the viewpoint of a character that we are used to seeing in King Arthur stories. It paints the characters we're used to seeing in a completely different light - I really ended up hating Lancelot in this series. All three books are well written and the story line keeps you turning those pages. I really, really enjoyed these novels.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10857731110197717463">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_492040246">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/492040246" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15984059-mr-matt" class="left imgcol" title="Mr. Matt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1401911574p2/15984059.jpg" alt="Mr. Matt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/492040246?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 01, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15984059-mr-matt" class="user" title="Mr. Matt">Mr. Matt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=hf-medieval-europe" class="actionLinkLite">hf-medieval-europe</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer492040246">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12424285565849329982">Simply one of the best historical fiction reads out there. A unique retelling of the Arthur legend as it may have really happened. Arthur is a Celtic warlord in a post-roman Britain. Merlin is a druid, but his magic is more of he slight of hand variety. The story takes place against a ripe backdrop of change - Romano-Celts versus invading Saxons and Angles and the new Christian God against the Old Gods. Great stuff. Highly recommended. </span>

          </span>
        </div>
